### B759 — False "someone else edited this in another tab" pop-up while actively editing in ONE tab (×2) `[Site Planner / persistence]` (bug) #site-planner #persistence #infra  *(owner-reported 2026-07-11 from chat — "While I was editing this building [Building 3, splitting a truck court off], I got a notification that someone else, or me in another tab, split it off — which can't be true, I'm only working in one tab. Figure out how that even happens." Branch `claude/concurrent-edit-notification-10br1m`. Minted **B757** via `npm run next-id`; RENUMBERED to **B759** = highest B# across both files (B758) + 1 on merge-in of `origin/main`, which took B757 (deleted-plan-resurrect) + B758 (bundle-404 white-screen) + V271/V272 — the code/tests/commit/branch keep the provisional **B757** label. → V273. **RECURRENCE 2026-07-13** (owner screenshot: a BURST of "you (another window) changed a paving area / trailer court you just edited — their version is showing", +2 more, all one tab) → **V301**; branch `claude/site-debugging-y82heo`.)*
`[x]` **FIXED this session — an adversarial 4-lens hunt + a red-team of the fix found FIVE single-tab self-echo false positives (3 realtime-read + 2 write-result timeout paths), each REPRODUCED live against the real `createElementSync` engine; all five fixed, 9 new regression tests + full suite green (3394) + `eslint` clean + build green. Red-team verdict on the fix: APPROVE-WITH-ADDITIONS (all additions folded in). The signed-in realtime end-to-end parks in ⏳ Verify → V273.**
- **Recurrence (×2, 2026-07-13) — the SIXTH self-echo path, in the no-pending READ branch the original fix's "read-path guards are SUFFICIENT" claim left open. FIXED this session** (repro'd against the real engine pre-fix; 4 new regression tests + guards; full suite **3696** green, `eslint` 0 errors, build green). Parks in ⏳ Verify → **V301** (same signed-in realtime class as V273).
  - **AUDIT-FIRST — root cause = `refetchReplace` re-seeds the shadow BACKWARD, then our own batch's echoes look foreign.** `SitePlanner.jsx refetchReplace` runs on EVERY socket (re)join, tab-wake, and the 4s fallback; it `await fetchElements(...)` at the top, then `eng.seed(rows)` (which `shadow.clear()`s and rebuilds). If that fetch's snapshot PREDATES a batch this tab just committed (fetch issued mid-edit-stream, seed runs after the commit lands), the seed rolls the shadow's revs BACKWARD. The just-committed batch's realtime echoes then arrive at a rev ABOVE the stale shadow with **no pending entry left** (dirty+inflight cleared on commit) → `applyRemoteRow`'s no-pending `remote-upsert` branch fires, and because we authored each element within the 15s window it stamps `authoredRecently:true` → one false "you (another window) changed X you just edited" per element = the owner's burst (a 6-element paving/trailer-court group edit → 6 toasts). B757's five fixes ALL live in the `if (pend)` branch + `processResults`; this branch had no own-echo guard. (The delete twin fires "…was deleted by you (another window)" the same way after a stale seed re-adds the row alive.)
  - **The fix (`lib/elementSync.js applyRemoteRow`, client-only, no schema change):** extend the SAME own-echo recognition B757 built into the pending branch to the no-pending read path. **Edit echo:** before emitting `remote-upsert`, if the incoming row's data byte-matches what THIS tab put on the wire in the last ~15s (`sentMatches`/`recentSent`), it's our own stale-seed echo → apply the canvas upsert (so a stale-seed canvas re-trues) but **suppress the conflict event** — no toast. **Delete echo:** a tombstone at a rev no newer than our own delete's remembered rev (the `tombstoned` floor) is our own delete echo → drop it from the canvas but suppress the event. Gated on DATA-identity / the delete floor, never on `updated_by` alone, so a genuine foreign write (different data / a rev above our delete) still surfaces per the B673 matrix.
  - **Named rules:** LIVE-VERIFY (signed-in realtime timing/race → V301); AUDIT-FIRST (traced the code to `refetchReplace`'s stale re-seed, reconciled against B757's "read-path guards sufficient" claim and found the gap); LOUD-FAILURE (self-echoes silenced by data-identity / delete-floor only — genuine conflicts stay loud, pinned by two GUARD tests). No `MAP.md` change (pure logic, no export change).
  - **Verified (sandbox):** a standalone node repro (`seed(fresh)→commit edit→seed(stale, older rev)→echo`) fired the false `remote-upsert(authoredRecently)` pre-fix, silent post-fix. `test/elementSync.test.js` +4: stale-seed edit echo → upsert, no toast; a genuine foreign upsert of a just-edited element STILL fires `remote-upsert(authoredRecently)`; stale-seed tombstone echo of our own delete → remove, no toast; a genuine foreign delete STILL fires `remote-delete`. All 43 elementSync tests green; full suite 3696 green.
  - **DEDUPE-FIRST:** this IS the recurrence of B759/B757 (same module `elementSync.js applyRemoteRow`, same symptom, same "you (another window)" resolver, same user goal) — reopened, not a new B#. The new path is the no-pending READ branch after a `refetchReplace` stale re-seed; B757 closed the pending + write-result paths only.
- Verify: live — signed-in, **timing/race + concurrency/multi-writer** class (mandatory LIVE-VERIFY); the engine logic is proven by unit repros/tests, but the false toast only manifests with a real Supabase realtime socket echoing a real commit, which the logged-out sandbox can't exercise. Owed on V273 (original 5 paths) + V301 (the recurrence's no-pending path).
- Origin: owner-reported 2026-07-11 (spurious concurrent-edit notification, single tab); recurrence owner-reported 2026-07-13 (burst screenshot).
- **AUDIT-FIRST — it's the NEW element-sync toast (B673), NOT the retired whole-doc "changed in another session" banner.** The wording the owner saw ("someone else… or me in another tab") is the B673 conflict toast whose editor name resolves to **"you (another window)"** for the user's own uid (`lib/editorNames.js`). The legacy doc-level banner was retired by architecture (B672 — slim header, no whole-doc payload to fight over), so this is a genuinely new false-positive in the per-element realtime read path.
- **Root cause (`lib/elementSync.js applyRemoteRow`): our OWN write echoing back over realtime is mis-read as a foreign edit.** Supabase realtime echoes a tab's own writes back to it; `applyRemoteRow` is the only guard, and it never checks `row.updated_by`/`deleted_by` against `selfUid` — it relies on (a) rev idempotency (`rev <= shad.rev`) and (b) a data-equality proxy (`sameData`). The realtime READ path (`applyRemoteRow`) had three holes; a red-team of the first fix then found two more on the WRITE-RESULT path (`processResults`) — **five** single-tab self-echo false positives, each reproduced live against the real `createElementSync` engine:
  1. **Edit-in-flight echo vs a newer queued edit (the reported one).** During active manipulation the echo of an in-flight commit (data **D1**, rev N+1) races ahead of its own RPC result, so the shadow rev is still N (< N+1) → the rev guard passes; meanwhile a **newer** edit (**D2**) queued into `dirty`, and the old code compared the echo only against the `dirty || inflight` **winner** (D2). D1 ≠ D2 → fired `remote-while-dirty` → *"you (another window) also just edited Building 3 — your version is being kept."*
  2. **Delete-in-flight tombstone echo.** Our own delete's tombstone echo (before its RPC result) can never satisfy `sameData` (the `!row.deleted_at` guard forces it false) → same false toast on a single-tab delete.
  3. **Stale post-delete echo RESURRECTS the element (worst — a data effect, not just a toast).** After editing then deleting an element, the delete's `shadow.delete()` removes the rev ceiling, so a delayed echo of the pre-delete UPDATE sails past every guard → `remote-upsert` puts the deleted element **back on the canvas** AND (authored within 15s) fires *"you (another window) changed … you just edited."*
  4. **Timed-out-but-committed EDIT (write-result path).** The 8 s `COMMIT_TIMEOUT_MS` aborts a commit that actually landed server-side; the retry re-flushes at the stale expected rev, hits OUR OWN committed row (a `conflict` whose `data` === our data), and `processResults` emitted `edit-vs-edit-lost-race` → *"was also just edited by you (another window) — your version was kept."*
  5. **Timed-out-but-committed RESTORE (write-result path).** Same mechanism on the Restore action → a false `restore-conflict` toast (*"already restored or edited by you (another window)"*).
  Splitting a truck court off a building is a multi-element create/move/delete gesture, so the read-path trio (1–3) can all fire at once; (4)/(5) need the rarer commit-timeout window.
- **The fix (`lib/elementSync.js`, client-only, no schema change):**
  - *(1) `applyRemoteRow` pending branch:* recognize the echo as OURS by matching the row against **either** pending serialization — the in-flight batch entry **and** the dirty entry (not just the winner) → adopt silently, no event.
  - *(2) pending branch:* a pending `delete` + an incoming tombstone is our own delete echo → silent.
  - *(3) new `tombstoned` map (key → {rev, at}):* on a committed delete, remember the delete's rev; a later non-tombstone echo at a rev **no newer** than that delete is a stale pre-delete self-echo → ignored (no resurrect, no toast). A genuine re-create by another session arrives at a **higher** rev, clears the floor, and comes through.
  - *(4)/(5) `processResults` conflict branches:* before emitting `edit-vs-edit-lost-race` / `restore-conflict`, if the conflicting live row's `data` **equals our own op's data**, it's our own timed-out-but-committed write echoing back → adopt the fresh rev silently, no re-commit, no toast. **Gated on data-equality, not `updated_by === selfUid` alone**, so a genuine same-account two-window conflict carrying *different* data still surfaces per the B673 matrix.
  - *(residual) new `recentSent` map (key → {json, at}):* the last serialization this tab put on the wire — it SURVIVES a transport-failure `inflight` clear, so a committed-but-unacked write's realtime echo is still recognized as ours even after `onTransportFailure` requeued a newer edit into `dirty`.
  All new memories are pruned to the 15 s window so they stay tiny. A genuine other-window write matches **neither** pending entry / carries **different** data / arrives **above** the delete floor, so real two-window conflicts still surface loudly; two writes that produce byte-identical data aren't a conflict anyway (the pre-existing `sameData`-adopt-silently semantics). No weakening of genuine multi-writer detection (a dedicated guard test pins this).
- **Why the read-path guards are SUFFICIENT on the success lifecycle:** the (1)/(2) window is exactly "echo passed `rev <= shad.rev`", true only while the commit is in flight (shadow not yet advanced). `inflightKeys` is cleared in the flush `finally` block in the SAME microtask as `processResults` advances the shadow rev — so the moment inflight clears, the rev guard already suppresses late echoes; the tombstone floor (3) covers the post-delete window, and `recentSent` covers the one exception (a `ok:false` transport failure clears inflight WITHOUT advancing the rev). The windows are complementary with no gap.
- **Named rules:** LIVE-VERIFY (signed-in timing/race + concurrency class → V273); AUDIT-FIRST (traced the code, ruled out the retired whole-doc banner, reconciled against the B672/B673 claims); TOMBSTONE-DELETES (the new tombstone floor extends the delete's authority so a stale echo can't resurrect); LOUD-FAILURE (self-echoes are silenced by data-identity, never by blanket-swallowing a class of events — genuine conflicts stay loud). Docs: no `MAP.md` change (no file add/remove/export change — pure logic inside `elementSync.js`).
- **Verified (sandbox):** four standalone node repros confirmed the reported bug + the delete/resurrection/timeout variants pre-fix and their absence post-fix. `test/elementSync.test.js` +9 regression tests — in-flight edit echo w/ newer queued edit → silent; in-flight delete tombstone echo → silent; stale post-delete edit echo → not resurrected; a genuine re-create above the delete rev still upserts; a genuine foreign edit (data ≠ inflight AND ≠ dirty) still fires `remote-while-dirty`; a timed-out-but-committed edit whose retry conflicts with our own row → silent; same for restore; a timed-out edit whose retry conflicts with DIFFERENT data still fires `edit-vs-edit`; a committed-but-unacked realtime echo after a newer edit queued during backoff → silent. All 39 elementSync tests green; full suite **3394** green; `eslint` clean; build green.
- **Note (the idempotency-key alternative):** paths (4)/(5) could alternatively be fixed with a per-op idempotency key on the `commit_elements` RPC (a live-DB change). The data-equality guard is the equivalent client-only fix (the server already returns the conflicting row's `data`), so no schema migration is needed and the whole class is closed in one branch.
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** NOT a recurrence of B612/B455/B460/B558/B596 (those are the retired whole-doc "changed in another session" banner). First filed false-positive in the B672/B673 per-element realtime toast path. Related-but-distinct from B672's V229 #5 (a lost-UPDATE data-loss on refetch); path #3 above is a spurious RESURRECTION, #1/#2/#4/#5 are spurious notifications.

### B758 — App white-screens when the MAIN bundle 404s during a deploy (no recovery exists for the entry chunk) `[App shell / infra]` (bug) #infra #ui  *(owner-reported 2026-07-11 from chat — "I pressed control shift r, and I guess we had just merged to change. And now the thing isn't even loading." Console showed `Failed to load resource: … 404 … index-CgI4uzRL.js`. Branch `claude/app-not-loading-merge-t7dwnu`. → V272.)*
`[x]` **FIXED this session — recovery mechanism proven headless (3-scenario browser test), build green; the real Cloudflare deploy-window race parks in ⏳ Verify → V272.** A hard reload during the seconds a fresh deploy was still propagating served the current `index.html` but 404'd its entry bundle `/assets/index-<hash>.js` at the owner's edge → blank white screen. **Confirmed transient:** that exact file returned HTTP 200 minutes later, and the live entry hash rolled `CgI4uzRL → DwgvooFK` (build id `6e67849`) between two checks — i.e. active deploy churn, not a broken build.
- Verify: live — deploy timing/race class (mandatory LIVE-VERIFY); the recovery mechanism is proven by a headless 3-scenario browser test, the real-deploy trigger is owed on V272.
- Origin: owner-reported 2026-07-11 (app not loading after a merge).
- **AUDIT-FIRST — why the existing recovery couldn't help.** `src/app/chunkReload.js` + `ErrorBoundary` already recover from stale/missing **lazy** workspace chunks (via Vite's `vite:preloadError`) and from render crashes — but that code lives INSIDE the main bundle. When the ENTRY bundle itself 404s, **no app JS runs at all**, so none of that machinery exists → a permanent white screen until a manual reload. The `_headers` (index.html `no-cache`, `/assets/*` immutable) and Cloudflare's atomic deploys are correct; the one uncovered gap is the brief edge-propagation window where fresh HTML points at a not-yet-published entry chunk.
- **The fix (`index.html`, inline boot watchdog — the entry-bundle analogue of B221/B239):** a small self-contained script that is part of index.html (the one file that is never content-hashed, so it never 404s and survives the failure). It catches **(A)** a definitive load error on the entry `<script>` (capture-phase `error` listener, filtered to a not-yet-mounted app + an `/assets/*.js` script so a font/CSS/image error or a late runtime throw never trips it) and **(B)** a never-mounts timeout, then shows an honest "Updating Planyr…" message and does a BOUNDED, cache-busting reload (`?_r=<ts>` — the same param the app already strips post-boot via `stripReloadParam`) to pick up the finished deploy. Bounded to **3** auto-reloads on a definitive load error (**1** on a bare mount-timeout, so a slow-but-fine connection isn't re-downloaded to death), then an honest "finishing an update / Try again" manual screen — never an infinite loop. A successful mount **clears the retry counter** so a future, separate deploy gets a fresh budget. Bails on `navigator.webdriver` (e2e/ui-audit untouched) and the whole body is `try/catch`, so it can never itself block boot.
- **Named rules:** LOUD-FAILURE (a blank dead page becomes a visible "updating" state + bounded auto-recovery, never a silent no-op). No pure lib touched (inline HTML), so no unit test is applicable — verified instead by a headless browser integration test.
- **Verified (sandbox — headless Chromium against a local server that serves `dist/` and 404s the entry bundle for the first N loads, `navigator.webdriver` overridden to false + a `#`-hash deep-link so the app boots like a real user):** (1) **normal boot** — 1 load, app mounts, overlay never appears, no leftover state; (2) **transient race healing after 2 failed loads** — 404 → auto-reload → 404 → auto-reload → 200 → app mounts, counter cleared (the owner's exact scenario); (3) **persistent break** — exactly 3 auto-reloads (4 total loads) then the honest manual-retry overlay, no loop. All three PASS. Build green.
- **Live check owed (V272):** on planyr.io after this deploys — confirm normal boot is unaffected (the watchdog is invisible on success), and (DevTools → Network → block `/assets/index-*.js` → reload) confirm the "Updating Planyr…" overlay appears and recovers when unblocked. A real Cloudflare deploy-race can't be forced on demand from the sandbox.

### B757 — Deliberately-deleted PLAN can resurrect on reload/sign-in when its cloud delete never landed (offline / transient) — no DURABLE record-delete tombstone `[Site Planner / Persistence]` (bug — data-integrity) #site-planner #persistence  *(chat 2026-07-11, from an adversarial-review brief — "NEW-4 (batch 2): deleted plan resurrects after a failed/unlanded cloud delete". Minted **B757** via `npm run next-id`. Branch `claude/backlog-sharing-realtime-site-ioc65x`.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED this session — sandbox verified (7 new unit tests, full suite 3,391 green, build green, lint 0 errors); the signed-in offline/cross-device round-trip parks in ⏳ Verify → V271.** A deliberate whole-plan delete now sticks across reload / sign-in / device sync instead of coming back.
- Verify: live — offline + cross-device delete durability is a mandatory LIVE-VERIFY class (concurrency / multi-writer timing). The pure suppression/retry logic is unit-proven; the real "delete offline → reload signed-in → still gone" is owed on V271.
- Origin: filed 2026-07-11 from the two-batch review brief; **most of that brief was already handled** (see the DEDUPE note below) — this residual is the one genuinely-open data-integrity gap it surfaced.
- **AUDIT-FIRST — the reported premises were HALF stale; the real gap is narrower and confirmed in code.** `cloudDelete` ALREADY does an affected-row check (`.delete().eq("id",id).select("id")` → typed `interpretDelete`, `cloudSync.js`), `deleteSite` ALREADY awaits it and `deleteSiteGroup` surfaces a LOUD "may reappear" on a failure / 0-row no-op (B372/B468). What was missing: the B372 guard is the **in-memory, per-tab `recentlyDeleted` Set** — cleared on reload and consulted **only in `saveSite`**. It does NOT stop `pullCloud` → `mergePulledSites` from RE-ADDING a cloud row whose delete never landed. So: signed-in, go offline, delete a plan → local removal + the loud warning, but on the next reload/sign-in the surviving cloud row is re-inserted (`map[id] = local ? merge : n`) → the plan is back. B372 fixed the same-session mount-flush half; this is the cross-reload/offline half it explicitly deferred.
- **The fix (`lib/storage.js` + a tiny `onStore` filter):** durable per-user `{id: ts}` tombstones (`planarfit:sites:deltomb:v1:<uid>`, bounded to 300). `deleteSite` records one; `mergePulledSites(existing, cloud, uid, tombstones)` now (a) SUPPRESSES an **owned** cloud row still pending removal (drops it from the merge → no resurrection) and flags it for retry, (b) KEEPS a row whose cloud copy is genuinely NEWER than the delete (`updatedAt > ts` = a real later edit on another device → the delete is stale — cross-device safety, mirrors B18/B511), (c) drops the tombstone for a not-ours (teammate) row or one the cloud already removed; `pullCloud` clears the honored tombstones and **RETRIES `cloudDelete`** for the pending ones, clearing each only on a confirmed removal. Nothing is dropped for a NON-tombstoned id — the change is byte-identical to today whenever no tombstone applies (unit-pinned).
- **Named rules:** TOMBSTONE-DELETES (a deliberate delete records a durable tombstone for the FULL record so a merge/sync can't resurrect it); LOUD-FAILURE (the existing "may reappear" banner stays; the retry now actually makes it land); LIVE-VERIFY (offline/cross-device timing → V271).
- **Also fixed (same delete/sync-hardening theme):** (1) **Doc Review `deleteReview`** now does the SAME `.select("id")` row-count check (`reviewStore.js`) — it previously reported `ok:true` on a 0-row no-op (silent survivor); it returns `removed` now, matching the sites path. (2) **`onStore` cross-tab filter** now excludes the `:history:` and `:deltomb:` sub-namespaces — the `planarfit:sites:` prefix also matched the version-history ring, so every default save ran the signed-out cross-tab fold 2–3× per edit (harmless no-op via the B591 signature check, but wasteful); tightened to the actual store keys.
- **Verified here (sandbox):** `test/storage.test.js` +7 (suppress owned-pending; keep-on-newer-cross-device; clear-on-landed; don't-suppress-teammate; never-drop-non-tombstoned; backward-compat with no tombstones) · full suite 3,391 green · build green · lint 0 errors · `MAP.md` regenerated (new `recordSiteTombstone`/`clearSiteTombstone` exports).
- **⏳ V271 (live, signed-in):** on planyr.io — delete a plan while offline (DevTools Offline), reload signed-in → the plan STAYS gone (and the cloud row is actually removed once back online); a plan legitimately edited on device B after being deleted on device A survives (cross-device exception). See VERIFICATION.md.
- **DEDUPE-FIRST — the rest of the two-batch brief maps to already-shipped work (no new numbers minted for these):** batch-1 NEW-1 (share never sets team_id) + NEW-2 (realtime RLS "leak") = **B714** (⏳ V244; share DOES set team_id — the bug was autosave reverting it, fixed; realtime is RLS-gated by schema, no leak); NEW-3 (cold-start `reading 'length'` crash) = **B690** (Done) + **B692** (⏳ V232 root-cause sanitize); NEW-4 (offline element lost-update, "reproduced twice") = the **B672** V229 #5 recurrence (fixed) + **B673/B674/B756**. Batch-2: NEW-2 (writeSites strips only underlay) = STALE (B473/B474 shed all three raster homes); NEW-3 (cloud push skipped on local-write fail) = **B473** (`pushModelToCloud`); NEW-5 (phantom "reload before saving" from a fold) = STALE (the B672 architecture retired that banner + the signed-in fold); NEW-6 (wire tombstones into all delete handlers) = **B556/B569/B596/B598/B612** (done). NEW-1 (autosave re-serializes the whole account — a real perf enhancement, not a bug) folded into **B479** as a bullet.

### B756 — DATA LOSS: a new signed-in site created from the map ("Plan N parcels →") silently loses ALL its parcels `[Site Planner / persistence]` (bug) #site-planner #persistence #infra  *(owner-reported 2026-07-10 from chat — "I deleted [the Bane site], selected all the same parcels, clicked start plan, it created the plan but then all my parcels went away." Branch `claude/parcels-disappear-plan-bug-iofgka`. → V270 renumbered from V269 on merge-in of `origin/main`, which took V269 for the parcel outline-style editor.)*
`[x]` **FIXED this session — sandbox + integration verified (10 new unit/integration tests, full suite green, build green); the signed-in end-to-end parks in ⏳ Verify → V270.** Confirmed live in Supabase: the reported site `smrfgk3pz3ii` "27211 Hoyt LN, Katy" has 0 parcel rows, 0 tombstones, 0 `site_elements` rows total — the parcels were **never committed**, then wiped. Same 0/0/0 loss on GREEN RIVER, HOLLISTER, WAYSIDE (all created after the 2026-07-06 cutover); every pre-cutover site kept its parcels.
- Verify: live — signed-in, timing/race + concurrency/multi-writer class (mandatory LIVE-VERIFY); the pure fold + engine-commit wiring is proven by unit/integration tests, the real signed-in "Plan parcels → reload → rows exist" end-to-end is owed on V270.
- Origin: owner-reported 2026-07-10 (data loss on new sites planned from the map).
- **AUDIT-FIRST — REGRESSION from the B672 read cutover, not the delete.** The delete-then-replan the owner described is INCIDENTAL; the causal flow is "create a new site from the map while signed in." Since B672 (commit `83411c8`, 2026-07-06, entrenched by `ec7b9fc` 2026-07-07) signed-in reads are canonical from the `site_elements` table and `slimForCloud` strips all 5 element collections out of the cloud `sites.data` header. But `newSiteFromMap` (`SitePlannerApp.jsx`) only writes the parcels to localStorage + that slim header — **nothing commits a brand-new site's initial parcels to `site_elements`** (`explodeModel` has zero runtime callers; no DB trigger explodes the blob). On first planner mount, `refetchReplace` (`SitePlanner.jsx`) fetches 0 rows, rebuilds `next.parcels=[]` (rows-canonical), and `setParcels([])` **wipes the canvas BEFORE** the seed-gated write engine (`reconcile()` is a no-op until `seed()`, which runs only inside `refetchReplace`) could ever diff/commit them; the follow-on autosave then `writeMirror()`s the empty state over localStorage too. Net: 0 rows, empty header, empty mirror → every parcel gone. It's a genuine race (some new sites survived only because the user re-drew shapes after the silent wipe, which then committed).
- **The fix (`SitePlanner.jsx refetchReplace` + a pure helper in `lib/elementRows.js`):** `foldNeverSyncedLocal(next, stateRef.current, rowKeys, isHuskParcel)` folds NEVER-SYNCED local-only elements — those on the pre-replace canvas whose `(kind,id)` has NO row at all (checked against LIVE **and** TOMBSTONE rows) — back into `next` before the replace, so they survive AND the existing `eng.reconcile(merged)` enqueues them as creates → they finally reach `site_elements`. Bounding the fold to zero-row `(kind,id)`s is what keeps it safe: anything that already has a row is left untouched, so rows stay canonical.
- **Named rules:** LOUD-FAILURE (a silent empty-save passed the B473/B592 count/membership check because want==got==0 — this closes that hole for new sites); TOMBSTONE-DELETES (a remotely-deleted element has a tombstone row → excluded from the fold → never resurrected); LIVE-VERIFY (signed-in race class → V270). Docs: `MAP.md` regenerated same commit (new `foldNeverSyncedLocal` export).
- **Verified (sandbox):** `test/elementRows.test.js` +8 (fold keeps a never-synced local parcel; adopts a live row; never resurrects a tombstone; drops husks; no dup; all 5 collections; `(kind,id)` keying vs the legacy e6327 class; input-immutability) and `test/elementSync.test.js` +2 integration (seed([]) + fold + reconcile → exactly one `create` commit; a row-backed stale local copy is NOT re-committed — V229 preserved). Full suite green, build green.
- **Safety vs V229 #5 (the exact clobber the cutover added `refetchReplace` to prevent):** a reconnecting stale tab holds old geometry ONLY for elements that already have rows → those `(kind,id)`s are in `rowKeys` → excluded from the fold → row adopted, never a stale rev-guarded re-commit. The fold can only ever emit *creates* for ids the server has literally never seen.
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** recurrence-of-CLASS of **B473** (Done — "a NEW site's edits vanish on reload when signed in"), whose regression guard `ui-audit/verify-new-site-save.mjs` runs LOGGED-OUT ONLY, which is exactly why the B672 cutover reopened new-site data loss undetected. Filed as a NEW B# (not a B473 reopen) because the mechanism is entirely new (the row cutover, not the blob path). Overlaps **B692** (husk-parcel funnel — same `refetchReplace` husk-filter code); the fold reuses `isHuskParcel` so a husk is never folded.
- **Owner note (recovery):** the fix stops all FUTURE loss. Already-lost sites (Katy/GREEN RIVER/HOLLISTER/WAYSIDE) have no cloud copy of their parcels; the just-planned Katy site is trivially re-created (re-select parcels → Plan). See V270 / OWNER-TODO for whether older ones held work worth recovering from a device's local version history.

### B625 — Metes-and-bounds deed rotates grossly off-angle on "Align to county parcel" (×2) `[Site Planner]` (bug) #site-planner #coordinates #gis  *(owner-reported 2026-07-02 on Grand Port; original fix shipped that session. RECURRENCE filed 2026-07-10 from chat (Cowork "NEW-1") — the align tool now over-rotates. Reopened per DEDUPE-FIRST / recurrence rule (B636) rather than minting a new B#; branch `claude/metes-bounds-rotation-bug-x58zih`.)*
`[x]` **RE-FIXED this session (recurrence) — sandbox + headless verified; the real-deed/real-parcel end-to-end parks in ⏳ Verify → V197.** The B625 align feature swung a plotted deed to a gross angle (tens of degrees, "~45°") instead of the intended small (~1.5°) basis-of-bearings correction, so it didn't overlay.
- Verify: live — repro cites real county-parcel project data + GIS import (mandatory LIVE-VERIFY class); the pure alignment math is proven by unit tests, the signed-in real-deed end-to-end is owed on V197.
- Recurrence: 2026-07-10 — owner (Cowork, "NEW-1"): a 67.63-ac deed lands over the 67.004-ac county parcel but badly rotated; a 42.32-ac deed floats with no parcel under it and still gets rotated.
- **AUDIT-FIRST — real cause (the reporter's projection / sign-flip / units leads were ruled OUT):** the bearing→vector parser (`metesAndBounds.js` `bearingToAz`/`callsToPath`) is correct (azimuth CW-from-north, dx=sin, dy=−cos, y-down), and deed rings + county rings (`arcgis.js lngLatRingToFeet`) share the SAME y-down feet frame — no sign/mirror bug. The gross rotation came from `deedAlign.js solveDeedAlignment`: it found the rotation by a **full ±180° sweep** minimizing a correspondence-free symmetric nearest-vertex RMS with scale locked to 1, so a near-symmetric / generalized outline snapped to a spurious 45/90/180° alias (the `confident` gate checks residual only, never rotation magnitude). `bestDeedFit` (`SitePlanner.jsx`) compounded it by force-fitting to the lowest-residual parcel even when none corresponded (the floating 42-ac case).
- **The fix (two parts):** (A) `deedAlign.js` — bound the rotation sweep and its clamped refine to a physically-plausible window `MAX_ALIGN_ROT_DEG = 20°` (covers grid convergence ~1.5° + record/magnetic basis slop; excludes the aliases); a deed that only fits past the window is reported not-confident, never force-rotated (reversed winding needs no wide sweep — the point-set metric handles it). (B) `SitePlanner.jsx bestDeedFit` — a spatial-correspondence gate (deed must overlap the parcel by ≥ half the smaller footprint via `polyIntersectArea`, AND their areas within ~4:3) so a non-corresponding parcel can't hijack the fit; with none qualifying it falls back to the small, safe grid-convergence correction / "no parcel" message, and the post-plot banner no longer false-claims an offset.
- **Tests:** `test/deedAlign.test.js` — 3 new (13 total): a near-symmetric deed rotated ~1.5° recovers ~1.5° not a 90° alias (would FAIL under the old ±180° sweep — the exact regression); a 45°-off deed clamps to ≤20° + reports not-confident; the `opts.maxRotDeg` override is honoured. Full suite **3302 green** · lint 0 errors · build green · `MAP.md` regenerated (new `MAX_ALIGN_ROT_DEG` export).
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** this IS the recurrence of B625 (same feature / module / symbols / user goal). Related, NOT dupes: `alignToParcelEdge` (element-edge snapper, bails on polygons) · `overlayAlign.solveSimilarityLSQ` (scanned-overlay similarity fit, a separate system) · B626 (the stale-sliver *parse*, resolved).

### B755 — Floodplain mitigation reads UNKNOWN because it won't calculate a BFE — auto-DERIVE one from FEMA's Base Flood Elevation lines `[Site Planner / GIS · yield]` (feature) #site-planner #gis #yield #floodplain  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-10 with the Bain/Concept A screenshot — "it's not calculating a base flood elevation, so it's not really doing anything useful for me … it should calculate a base flood elevation. `[x]` **IMPLEMENTED this session — sandbox+headless verified (24 new mitigation + 4 new pipeline unit tests, all green; app boots clean); the real-Bain-GIS derive + the priced volume it produces park in ⏳ Verify → V268.** The mitigation engine needs a 1% BFE to price compensating storage, but FEMA leaves `STATIC_BFE` at the −9999 sentinel on most AE polygons, so the readout honestly dead-ended at "no published BFE on this reach."
- Verify: live
- Origin: filed 2026-07-10 from chat (owner drop)
- **AUDIT-FIRST — the BFE genuinely wasn't on the polygon we queried.** Confirmed against the live FEMA NFHL for the Bain reach (29.7701, −95.8502): the AE zone's `STATIC_BFE` IS −9999, but the BFE lives on the SEPARATE **S_BFE line layer (NFHL sublayer 16)** — 24 whole-foot contour lines (133–146 ft, all Feet/NAVD88) cross the site — which the app never fetched. `assessHydraulicRegime`/`computeMitigation` were correct to read UNKNOWN; the gap was a missing data source, not a bug.
- **Fix (new `bfe-line-interp` provider, slotted after manual, before UNKNOWN):**
  • **GIS pipeline** (`vectorLayers.js`) — `featuresToGeoJson` now emits LineString/MultiLineString from Esri `geometry.paths` (it silently dropped every line feature before — the fabricated-empty-result trap); `simplifyGeoJson` passes non-polygons through unthinned (thinning would shift a line off the query point); new `bfeLines` (sublayer 16) + `crossSections` (14, registered-not-consumed) sources.
  • **Derivation** (`floodplainMitigation.js`, pure) — `bfeLinesFromFeatureCollection` (feet+NAVD88 guard; −9999/NGVD29/meters excluded and counted — never a mixed-datum silent error) + `deriveBfeFromLines` (distance-weighted interpolation between the nearest line and the nearest DIFFERENT-elevation line — "read a spot elevation between two topo contours"; degrades to nearest-line ±0.5 ft, then to null → the existing honest UNKNOWN when no line is within 2500 ft).
  • **Wiring** (`SitePlanner.jsx`) — `checkDrainage` pulls S_BFE on the same explicit click + SWR cache and derives one BFE at the fill-footprint centroid; threaded through `fmElev.derivedBfeFt`, `fmGoverningBfe` (buildability/FFE), and the mit/pond memo sigs. It NEVER writes to `settings.floodMitigation.bfeFt` (would fake a manual entry); a published static BFE, an AO zone's grade+DEPTH, and a manual entry all still outrank it.
  • **Honest labeling (owner option A)** — priced off the central estimate with the conservative upper bracket shown alongside; Yield row tagged "BFE derived", FloodMitigationCard provider "derived (BFE lines)" + a note stating the interpolation, bracket, and "screening estimate — confirm before design; type a BFE to override"; BFE input placeholder shows "~x derived"; print sheet appends "(derived BFE — screening est.)".
- **Named rules:** LOUD-FAILURE (the polyline-drop trap fixed; a failed/empty/out-of-range pull → honest UNKNOWN, never a fabricated number), AUDIT-FIRST (reconciled against the existing STATIC_BFE path — the −9999 was real), PDF-PARITY (export mirrors the derived tag). Docs: `MAP.md` regenerated same commit (new exports).

Not a recurrence — the B707 regime/mitigation engine + its "no published BFE" honesty are the base this EXTENDS (it fills exactly that gap); cross-sections (WSEL_REG) and HCFCD MAAPnext are deliberately deferred (v2; the S_XS source is registered, not consumed).

### B751 — Detention: make the HCFCD-channel-drainage + reviewing-agency assumptions transparent AND user-overridable, and remember the last drainage check `[Site Planner / GIS · yield]` (bug+feature) #site-planner #gis #yield #persistence  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-10 with a screenshot of the Bain/Concept A Stormwater readout — "why is it unknown whether the site drains into a[n] HCFCD channel when one literally runs through the middle of the site … it should let me know whether it assumes this or not … I can click a checkbox and tell it … and why does it not know whether it's City of Houston or Harris County flood control district if I have an analysis tool that can detect that?" `[x]` **IMPLEMENTED this session — sandbox+headless verified (13 new unit tests + 8 new headless assertions, all green); the real-GIS channel naming on a live Harris/COH site + cross-session persistence on the SIGNED-IN app park in ⏳ Verify → V264.** Two transparency+control gaps, not missing detection.
- Verify: live
- Origin: filed 2026-07-10 from chat (owner drop)
- **AUDIT-FIRST — the detection already existed.** `resolveDrainageContext` already queries the real HCFCD channel centerline layer (`HCFCD/Channels/MapServer/0`) → `channel.near`, and resolves COH-vs-HCFCD via `identifyJurisdiction`. The panel fed `drainsToHcfcdChannel: drainCtxData?.channel?.near ?? null` with NO user override, so when the HCFCD host was unreachable (or the visible channel isn't an HCFCD unit) `near` came back `null` and the tool hedged "…is unknown," dead-ending the user. And the rule badge showed the governing-RATE authority (HCFCD) while the greater-of named Houston — reading as indecision when it's actually Houston's own >20-ac rule.
- **Fix (both owner-chosen options):**

State-aware plain-English copy names the detected unit ("HCFCD channel detected — Unit W100-00-00 … assuming your detention discharges to it"), or on a failed lookup "Couldn't confirm from HCFCD's map server … set Yes or No," or on override the confirmed copy.

  • **Greater-of clarity** — names the reviewing authority ("City of Houston, detected from city-limits GIS") DISTINCTLY from the governing rate ("For a tract over 20 acres, Houston applies the larger of its own rate and HCFCD's — … so HCFCD's N ac-ft governs"), so it no longer reads as indecision.
  • **"Remember it"** — a slim, geometry-free summary of the last check + the two override choices persist in `settings.drainage` (rides the existing settings autosave — NO schema/version bump); on reload the readout shows last-known facts with a "Remembered from your last check on <date> — re-check to refresh" line.
- **Pure helpers (new, unit-tested):** `effectiveChannelDischarge`, `effectiveReviewer`, `DETENTION_AUTHORITY_CHOICES`, `slimDrainageContext`/`hydrateDrainageContext` (round-trip: rule + watershed overlays re-derived, geometry dropped) in `lib/detentionRules.js`. The engine's `drainsToHcfcdChannel` true/false/null branches were already tested.
- **Deliberate boundary (not changed):** the owner/primary-source-verified rule that a >20-ac COH tract defers to HCFCD's rate even on "No" (COH IDM Table 9.5, V204) is surfaced + explained, not re-calibrated — a "No drops it to Houston-rate-only" change would be a separate rule decision.
- **Named rules:** LOUD-FAILURE (a failed channel/jurisdiction lookup shows an honest hedge + the override, never a silent all-clear), AUDIT-FIRST (reconciled against the existing detection engine — extend, not fork), MODULE-SCOPE-COMPONENTS (controls are inline JSX, no inner component). ### B754 — Detention: a City-of-Houston **ETJ** parcel was wrongly treated as City-of-Houston for detention criteria `[Site Planner / GIS · yield]` (bug) #site-planner #gis #yield  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-10 on the Bain/Concept A readout — "Why does it think this site goes to the city of Houston? Minted this session as **B752**; RENUMBERED to **B754** = highest B# across both files (B753) + 1 on merge-in of `origin/main`, which took B752/B753 + V265/V266 for the pipeline vector-rendering feature — the code comments/tests/commit keep the provisional **B752** label. Follows B751, which introduced the "detected from city-limits GIS" wording that exposed this latent mis-routing.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED this session — sandbox+headless verified (unit tests + a new headless spec `verify-etj-detention.mjs`, all green); the live-GIS confirm on the real 27211 Hoyt Ln (Katy) site on the SIGNED-IN app parks in ⏳ Verify → V267.** Being inside a city's ETJ means the city reviews the PLAT, but the COUNTY drainage district's criteria GOVERN detention — it must NOT set the detention reviewer to that city.
- Verify: live
- **AUDIT-FIRST — verified the repro against the LIVE GIS via curl at the parcel's coordinates (29.7722, -95.8548):** city-limits layer (TxGIO) returns **empty** (NOT in any city), the H-GAC ETJ layer returns **HOUSTON**, the county layer returns **Fort Bend**. So the parcel is unincorporated Fort Bend land inside Houston's ETJ. The bug: `authorityForJurisdiction` (`lib/detentionRules.js`) routed `cities.includes("houston") || etjs.includes("houston")` → `primary="coh"`, so an ETJ-only hit set the reviewer to City of Houston, and the UI hardcoded "(detected from city-limits GIS)" — doubly wrong (it was an ETJ hit, and the city-limits layer says nothing there). Root cause predates B751 (lived in B93/B629); B751's new wording surfaced it.
- **Fix:** ETJ membership WITHOUT actual city-limits membership no longer sets `primary` to `coh`. The COUNTY drainage authority governs (Fort Bend → FBCDD here), and the Houston-ETJ status is surfaced as an informational `overlays` note + `houston-etj` flag: *"This parcel is in the City of Houston ETJ …, not its city limits. Houston reviews the plat, but the COUNTY drainage-district criteria govern detention here — Houston's own detention rate does not apply. Verify with both the City and the county."* Rendered in the Yield/Stormwater readout (`d.etjNotes`). The genuine in-city-limits Houston path (`cities.includes("houston")`) is unchanged, so the >20-ac greater-of + "detected from city-limits GIS" wording now fire ONLY for real city-limits parcels. Removed the now-false `appliesInEtj:true` rule param + rewired the `jurisdiction-partial` flag (a failed ETJ query can no longer imply a hidden City answer; only a failed CITY-limits query can).
- **Named rules:** AUDIT-FIRST (reconciled the claim against the live endpoints before patching), LOUD-FAILURE (the ETJ note is explicit, never a silent re-label), MODULE-SCOPE-COMPONENTS (inline JSX note, no inner component).
- **Verified (sandbox):** `test/detentionResolver.test.js` updated (Houston-ETJ→county authority + `houston-etj` flag; Fort-Bend-ETJ→`fortbend`; ETJ-outage no longer flags partial), full suite **3308** green, build green; new `ui-audit/verify-etj-detention.mjs` (Fort Bend + Houston-ETJ, no city limits) → reviewer reads **Fort Bend County Drainage District**, never City of Houston, ETJ note present — 5/5 pass; existing `verify-b629-detention.mjs` COH pass (real city-limits) still green.

### B747 — Overlay tool accepts CAD files: client-side DXF import with true-units auto-scale `[Site Planner]` (feature) #site-planner #files  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-10 as "NEW-1"; the CAD follow-on B67/B72 explicitly deferred. Minted **B747** = highest B# across both files (B746) + 1.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED this session — sandbox+headless verified; the true-units/large-file/reload paths that need a signed-in live app park in ⏳ Verify → V260.** Extend the B72 site-plan overlay to accept `.dxf` files alongside PDF/PNG/JPG, parsing off the main thread and auto-placing at true real-world size when the DXF declares its units.
- Verify: live
- Origin: filed 2026-07-10 from chat (owner NEW-1)
- **Entry point (reused, not forked):** `openOverlayFile` (`lib/overlayPdf.js`) gained an `isDxfFile` branch (extension `.dxf` OR a sniffed `0\nSECTION` header — MIME is unreliable for DXF); the one dropzone + file-picker `accept` list now includes `.dxf`. No second import path.
- **Parse:** one small parse-only dependency authorized + added — **`dxf-parser`** (1 transitive dep `loglevel`, ~380 KB; justification recorded in `/CLAUDE.md` dependency notes). Runs in a dedicated **Web Worker** (`lib/dxf/dxfWorker.js`, import-list test-guarded like `terrainWorker`) so a big drawing never freezes the tab.
- **Render:** hand-rolled entity→SVG for the civil subset — LINE, LWPOLYLINE/POLYLINE (incl. **bulge arcs**), ARC, CIRCLE, ELLIPSE, TEXT/MTEXT (basic placement, no font fidelity), INSERT (blocks expanded recursively with nested transforms). Unsupported entity types are **counted and surfaced** ("Imported — N entities of unsupported types skipped"), never silently dropped. The SVG rasterizes to a transparent PNG at high resolution → feeds the existing `{src, imgW, imgH}` overlay shape and inherits every move/scale/rotate/opacity handle, `sheetOverlays` rendering, and print/export path unchanged.
- **True-units auto-scale (the payoff):** read `$INSUNITS`. Units known (ft/in/m/mm/cm/…) → compute `ftPerPx` exactly from model-space extents, auto-placed at true size (no B73 calibration needed). `$INSUNITS = 0` (unitless) → assume feet (correct for ~all Texas civil work) but flag visibly on the panel ("Units assumed: feet — verify") with B73's Trace-a-length / scale controls offered inline. Never a silent guess without the flag.
- **Persistence:** original `.dxf` stored via `overlayStorage.uploadOverlayFile` (`fileKind` extended with `dxf`; 50 MB Storage ceiling applies and oversize now **fails visibly** — a warn banner, per LOUD-FAILURE); raster is a regenerable cache exactly like the PDF path (`slimForCloud` strips it; the reload effect re-renders from stored bytes via a new `rasterizeStoredDxf` branch beside PDF/image).
- **Tests:** unit tests for the entity→SVG geometry (bulge-arc math, INSERT transform composition, `$INSUNITS`→`ftPerPx`, unsupported counting) with small fixture DXFs; headless Playwright drop-a-DXF smoke.
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** searched Open/⏳/Done for `dxf`·`dwg`·overlay import. **B72** = drop a PDF/image + place by hand; **B73** = scale calibration/trace; **B238** = the DWG→DXF *backend*; **B364** = Doc-Review *filing* read of scanned/DWG (a different module + purpose). No prior **DXF overlay-import** item — net-new, the CAD follow-on B67/B72 deferred.

### B749 — Overlay PDF rasterization quality: raise base resolution + zoom-aware re-raster `[Site Planner]` (feature) #site-planner #perf  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-10 as "NEW-3". Minted **B749** = B748 + 1.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED this session — zoom-/data-density-dependent rendering is a mandatory LIVE-VERIFY class → parks in ⏳ Verify → V262.** Placed PDF overlays went soft when zoomed past sheet-fit because `rasterizePage` capped the raster at `MAX_RASTER_DIM = 2600 px`.
- Verify: live
- Origin: filed 2026-07-10 from chat (owner NEW-3)
- **Tier 1 — raise the base:** `MAX_RASTER_DIM` → **4500** (scale cap lifted so small sheets sharpen too), with a **row-banded** white-knockout pass so the `getImageData` transient stays bounded at 4500 px (the existing tolerant tainted-canvas catch is kept). Base raster stays a persisted **data URL** (the safety-critical strip/reload/cloud chain is deliberately untouched — zero data-loss regression).
- **Tier 2 — zoom-aware re-raster:** when the overlay's on-screen magnification exceeds ~1.5× its raster pixels, re-render that PDF page at a higher scale (cap **8192 px**, the common GPU texture limit) from the in-session pdf proxy (or, after reload, from stored bytes via `rasterizeStoredPdf`), debounced behind zoom-settle, swapped in place on the SAME transform (placement is anchored to intrinsic PDF points, so resolution changes never move/resize it). The hi-res raster is a **transient revocable object URL** held in a ref (the B45 precedent) — never persisted, never in undo/state bloat — and is dropped back to the base raster + revoked when zoomed out, so multiple hi-res overlays can't accumulate in memory.
- **Not in scope / dedupe:** Doc-Review's separate render-sharpness / white-flash items (B45 object-URL, B414/B415 double-buffer) — this is the **Site Planner overlay path only**; not merged with those.
- **Tests:** unit tests for the scale-selection math (viewport magnification → chosen raster scale, 8192 cap respected, downgrade threshold).

### B750 — Clicking an element auto-opened its Properties menu; make single-click SELECT and double-click OPEN Properties `[Site Planner / Doc Review]` (feature) #site-planner #doc-review #selection #ui #markup  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-10 from chat: "I don't want clicking on any element to automatically open the properties menu — single left click selects, double left click opens the properties menu." Branch `claude/properties-menu-click-behavior-dkmh1i`.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED + unit + headless-e2e verified (Site Planner) this session; parks in ⏳ Verify only for the Doc Review live click-through → V263.** Previously the Properties companion was DERIVED from the selection (`companionSel`), so a plain click popped it open. Now selection and "show Properties" are decoupled: a single click SELECTS only; a **double-click opens Properties**. Text stays editable via the owner's rule — "click to select, then double-click to edit text": a double-click on an ALREADY-selected text-bearing feature (text callout, labeled line/polyline/easement, labeled centerline road) edits its text in place; any other double-click opens Properties. The type/actions menu moved off double-click and stays on **right-click**. Applies to both the Site Planner and the Review markup tool.
- Verify: live
- Origin: filed 2026-07-10 from chat
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** searched Open / ⏳ Verify / Done (`^### B` + `#selection`/`#ui`/`#markup`) — **net-new**. NOT B679 (double-click-to-edit-text — that gesture is PRESERVED here as the already-selected exception), NOT B733 (the docked Properties *tab*, which still opens the inspector for the current selection regardless of the new marker), NOT B740 (shift-click multi — reached via the Properties tab now).
- **Implementation:** `SitePlanner.jsx` — replaced the `propsDismissed` state with an explicit `propsFor` marker (`{kind,id}` | 'multi' | null); the companion renders only when it matches the current selection (`propsMatches`), so ANY non-double-click selection path (single click, marquee, shift-multi, programmatic, undo/redo) leaves it closed without touching the ~70 `setSel` sites. `isDoubleTap` gained a `wasSel` arg (captured on the first press, read via `dblWasSelRef`) so a double-tap can tell "already-selected text → edit text" from "→ open Properties". The three `startMove*` pointerdown handlers + `onElDouble` route accordingly; the canvas-shift calc, ✕ button, phone ✎ pill, and Properties-tab open were repointed off `propsDismissed`. `DocReview.jsx` — added a `propsForId` marker gating the rail Properties section (the armed-tool "Tool style" preview still shows), a `dblRef` capturing the first-press selection in `onDown`, `onDbl` disambiguates edit-text vs open-Properties, and a freshly DRAWN markup auto-opens Properties (its rail section would otherwise be blank).
- **Product decisions (owner-confirmed via AskUserQuestion):** double-click = properties everywhere, text edited via select-then-double-click; applies to both workspaces. Auto-open-on-DRAW is split by surface — **Review: yes** (its Properties is an always-present rail section; skipping it leaves a blank rail), **Site Planner: no** (its companion is a pop-over — the exact annoyance being removed; double-click or the Properties tab to style a fresh shape). Multi-selection reaches the shared style panel via the Properties tab. Reaching Properties of an already-selected TEXT feature = select something else and come back, or use the Properties tab (the literal consequence of the owner's text rule).
- **Verified (sandbox/headless):** updated the B679 source-text guard block in `test/bugHuntGuards.test.js` (new `isDoubleTap` signature + branches + `propsMatches`/new `companionOpen`/no-typeMenu-on-dblclick). New logged-out e2e `e2e/click-behavior.spec.js` (Site Planner, ran 3× stable): draw a building → companion CLOSED (no auto-open); double-click → Properties opens with its Delete-element control; ✕ closes it; single-click → stays closed (select only). `e2e/element-delete.spec.js` updated to open Properties via the docked **Properties** rail tab before the panel Delete (the panel no longer auto-opens on the drawn road's selection). Full unit suite green (3254) · full e2e green (43 passed, auth-gated skipped) · build green.
- **⏳ V263 (live/browser):** two gaps the sandbox couldn't cover — (a) **Review click-through** (the fixture PDF triggers an OCR pass and the page canvas wasn't ready to accept a drawn rectangle; the repo's own per-tool Review e2e is auth-gated for the same reason): open a drawing in Review → draw a rect → Properties auto-show → deselect → the Properties section is blank → single-click the rect → still blank → double-click → Properties show → double-click an already-selected TEXT note → the inline text editor opens (not the panel); (b) **Site Planner phone ✎ pill** on a narrow viewport still opens the companion (the e2e ran desktop only).

### B745 — Vector / thin-line GIS map layers (transmission, road-authority, county/city/ETJ boundaries, contours, drainage arrows, OSM/Mapillary) now composite into the PDF/PNG export `[Site Planner / GIS · export]` (feature) #site-planner #export #gis  *(split from B739 2026-07-10 — B739 shipped the raster/shaded class; this ships the vector/client-drawn class. → V259, bumped from V258 which a concurrent `main` merge (the Ctrl+Z item B746) took.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED + headless-verified this session; parks in ⏳ Verify (Verify: live — PDF/export-parity + GIS-endpoint classes; the sandbox can't reach the live agency hosts through the cert proxy, so the real per-layer geometry-paint needs a live click-through).** Completes the "everything I have on" print request. The thin-line layers are drawn client-side by Leaflet (SVG paths / canvas / markers inside the `data-export="skip"` map div), so — unlike the raster class — there's no server image to re-fetch. Each ENABLED vector layer's lat/lon geometry is read live from `overlayRefs`, **reprojected into the site feet frame (`lngLatRingToFeet` → `f2p`) and redrawn as styled SVG** into the export clone, composited at the SAME z-anchor as the raster overlays (above them, below the drawn geometry).

### B746 — Ctrl+Z doesn't always work; make it Bluebeam-style when drawing an element `[Site Planner / Doc Review]` (bug) #site-planner #doc-review #selection #markup #ui #persistence  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-10 from chat; provisional **B745**, renumbered **B746** — concurrent `main` (PR #566) took B745 for the GIS vector/thin-line export split + V257. Per repo precedent the commit keeps the provisional **B745** label; only the backlog + verification IDs bumped (→ B746 / V258). Branch `claude/ctrl-z-undo-behavior-552b1t`.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED + unit + headless-e2e verified this session; parks in ⏳ Verify only for the live-only edges below → V258.** Two complaints, one investigation (5-lens adversarial workflow, 15 confirmed root causes RC-1..RC-9): (a) **"Ctrl+Z should work like Bluebeam when drawing"** and (b) **"Ctrl+Z doesn't always work."** The Site Planner's Ctrl+Z always ran a *global* undo — it never stepped back the vertex you were placing — so mid-draw it either did nothing or silently reverted a previously-finished shape while the half-drawn one stayed on screen. Now, in all three canvases (Site Planner, Review, Stitcher), Ctrl+Z **peels the last placed vertex while a multi-point draft is in progress and only falls through to a global undo when no draft is active** (matches Bluebeam + the Review/Stitcher modules, which already did this). Plus a batch of "undo did nothing / undid the wrong thing" reliability fixes.
- Verify: live
- Origin: filed 2026-07-10 from chat
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** searched Open / ⏳ Verify / Done (BACKLOG*.md + BACKLOG_OPEN.md, `^### B` + `#selection`/`#markup`) — **net-new**. Related, NOT dupes: **B32/B105** (no-op history dedup — the engine this builds on), **B315** (undo read a stale baseline — the `stateRef` fix reused here), **B303** (Review's own mid-draw vertex step-back — the sibling pattern the Site Planner was missing), **B567** (color-pick one-frame session — the coalescing pattern extended to opacity sliders here).
- **AUDIT-FIRST — 9 code-confirmed root causes (each adversarially verified):**
  - **RC-1 (Bluebeam, primary):** `SitePlanner.jsx` Ctrl+Z called `undo()` directly, never `removeLastVertex()`. Fixed to `else if (!removeLastVertex()) undo();` (mirrors `DocReview.jsx` / `Stitcher.jsx`).
  - **RC-2:** `applySnapshot` didn't clear in-progress drafts → a redo/undo could leave phantom draft points floating over reverted geometry. Now nulls every draft (mirrors the siblings).
  - **RC-3:** `removeLastVertex` had no branch for the parcel-edge easement run (`easeEdges`) or the ditch cross-section point (`xsecPts`), and `xsecMode/xsecPts` were missing from the keydown deps → stale closure. Added both branches + deps.
  - **RC-4:** Split tool double-destruction (Ctrl+Z discarded the whole cut path AND reverted a prior action) — falls out for free once RC-1 lands (mid-split Ctrl+Z now peels one cut point). Verified gone.
  - **RC-5:** Edits that recorded NO undo frame — element fill-opacity slider, underlay opacity slider, sheet-overlay opacity slider + %-box, and **Remove aerial underlay**. Now each records exactly one frame.
  - **RC-6:** Standards / type-style edits called `pushHistory()` but `settings` isn't in the snapshot → a **dead frame** that misdirected the next Ctrl+Z into deleting a prior shape. Removed those pushes (Standards are prefs, non-undoable like the 20+ sibling settings fields) — no more misdirection.
  - **RC-7:** Markup fill-opacity slider *flooded* history (one frame per `onChange`) → ~20 Ctrl+Z to undo one drag. All opacity sliders now share one `sliderHistory` coalescing helper (one frame per drag).
  - **RC-8:** Sheet-overlay position was `Math.round`ed in `histKey`, so a sub-foot (zoomed-in) nudge was dedup'd away as a no-op and skipped by undo. Removed the rounding (underlay position never was).
  - **RC-9:** The keydown input-guard diverged — Review/Stitcher skipped only INPUT/TEXTAREA, so a focused `<select>`'s Ctrl+Z hit the canvas. Added SELECT/contentEditable so all three modules gate identically.
- **Fix (files):** `SitePlanner.jsx` (Ctrl+Z routing, `removeLastVertex`→pure resolver, `applySnapshot` draft-clear, `histKey` overlay precision, 5 opacity sliders + remove-underlay history, RC-6 dead-push removals, deps); new pure **`lib/drafts.js`** (`resolveDraftStepBack`); `DocReview.jsx` + `Stitcher.jsx` (RC-9 guard).
- **Verified (sandbox/headless):** new **`test/drafts.test.js`** (10 cases — every draft type incl. the two new ones + the "no draft → null" fall-through that keeps a real Ctrl+Z from being swallowed) · full unit suite green (3232) · `test/history.test.js` still green · build green · MAP.md regenerated (+`lib/drafts.js`) · **new `e2e/ctrlz-undo.spec.js` (3 tests, LOGGED-OUT via "Start blank", green in headless Chromium): mid-draw Ctrl+Z peels a vertex (finished polygon has 3 pts, not 5); mid-draw Ctrl+Z does NOT revert a previously-committed shape; no-draft Ctrl+Z is a real global undo + redo.**
- **⏳ V258 (live, planyr.io):** the few edges the logged-out sandbox can't confirm — (1) a **sub-foot sheet-overlay nudge at high zoom** undoes cleanly (RC-8, zoom-dependent-rendering class); (2) **Remove aerial underlay → Ctrl+Z restores it**, incl. the reload-after-undo persistence edge where the image was cloud/idb-backed (RC-5, signed-in persistence class); (3) opacity-slider undos that round-trip through Supabase/Drive persistence.

### B744 — "Drop site plan" overlay hint sticks after a drag leaves the window; make it non-obscuring `[Site Planner]` (bug) #site-planner #ui  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-09 as "NEW-1"; provisional **B736**, renumbered **B744** — fast-moving concurrent `main` took B734–B743 + V250–V255 across several merges. Per repo precedent the code/tests/commit keep the provisional **B736** label; only the backlog + verification IDs bumped (→ B744 / V256). Branch `claude/site-planner-overlay-bugs-yzkalh`.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED + headless-verified this session; parks in ⏳ Verify (Verify: live — HTML5/OS drag interaction; the real browser drag layer only reproduces live, the synthetic e2e proves the wiring) → V256.** The full-canvas "Drop site plan to place it on the map" drag hint could stay stuck ON after a file was dragged over the canvas and then back OUT of the browser window without dropping; and while shown its light-theme fill was opaque, hiding existing geometry. The highlight is now driven by a dragenter/dragleave DEPTH COUNTER + a window-level reset, and its fill is a translucent accent wash (both themes) so the site stays visible under it.
- Verify: live
- Origin: filed 2026-07-09 from chat
- **AUDIT-FIRST — the report's Part A does NOT reproduce.** The report described a "persistent full-canvas takeover that covers geometry + blocks clicks." It doesn't exist: the overlay (`SitePlanner.jsx` ~9453) mounts ONLY while `canvasDropOver` is true (an active file drag) and is already `pointerEvents:none`, so it never blocks a click and there is no persistent empty-state takeover (grep-confirmed: the exact hint string appears once; there is no other full-canvas prompt). **B445 already made it drag-gated + click-through.** Part A is therefore honored in *spirit* only — a non-obscuring translucent fill — not by gating a non-existent persistent overlay on emptiness.
- **Part B (the real defect):** the canvas wrapper's `onDragLeave` only cleared when `e.currentTarget === e.target` (false whenever the pointer was over the child `<svg>` at exit), and the window guard listened only for `dragover`/`drop` — NO window `dragleave`/reset. An OS-file drag fires no in-page `dragend`, and its final window-exit `dragleave` can target `document`/`body` (outside the wrapper subtree), so nothing cleared the flag → the tan highlight stuck on with nothing under the cursor.
- **Fix (`SitePlanner.jsx`):** (1) both dropzones (canvas wrapper + References panel) now use a per-zone dragenter/dragleave DEPTH COUNTER ref — highlight iff depth>0, force depth=0 on drop — robust against the child-crossing flicker (a child's bubbling `dragenter` fires before the parent's `dragleave`, so depth never dips to 0 mid-hover) and replacing the fragile `currentTarget===target` guard. (2) The window guard `useEffect` gains a `dragleave` listener that hard-resets ALL drag-hover flags + both counters, but ONLY when the drag truly left the window (`relatedTarget==null` **AND** pointer coords at/past a viewport edge — AND, **not the brief's OR**, because Chromium routinely reports a null `relatedTarget` on in-page moves too, so a bare OR would re-introduce the flicker), plus the window `drop` handler now also resets (catch-all for an aborted/missed drop). `preventDefault` on dragover (drop stays allowed) + the panel drop's `stopPropagation` are preserved. (3) Part A spirit: the hint fill is now `color-mix(in srgb, <accent> 18%, transparent)` in both themes (was opaque `canvasAccentSoft` in light) so geometry shows through; `pointerEvents:none` kept; the shared `canvasAccentSoft` token untouched.
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** searched Open / ⏳ Verify / Done — **distinct from B445 / V131** (which BUILT this affordance; shared symbols `canvasDropOver`, the window-guard `useEffect`, `verify-overlay-dnd.mjs`). This is a GAP in B445's edge-case reset (leave-window), NOT a regression — B445's drop/feedback fix still works — so per the repo's gaps-get-new-numbers convention (cf. B446 "GAP in B294", B450 "follow-up to B239") it takes a new number, not a B445 recurrence. Deed dropzone (`deedDrag`, in a modal) left as-is — it clears on any dragleave (never "stuck") and is now covered by the window reset.
- **Verified (sandbox/headless):** `ui-audit/verify-overlay-dnd.mjs` (logged-out, real built app on :4173) — **11/11**, including the three new B736 assertions: enter×2 (wrapper + bubbled child) then one child `dragleave` KEEPS the hint (no flicker) and clears only at depth 0; a window `dragleave` (`relatedTarget=null` + coords-outside) clears a stuck hint; a window `drop` preventDefaults + resets. Also repaired pre-existing harness drift (B654 renamed the rail "Overlay"→"References", the panel copy, and the overlay-row title). Full unit suite green (3161) · lint 0 errors · build green. (No MAP.md change — no files added/removed/renamed.)
- **⏳ V256 (live, on planyr.io):** the synthetic e2e proves the wiring deterministically, but a real desktop OS file-drag exercises the browser's native drag layer end-to-end. On planyr.io: (1) canvas with a parcel + placed metes-and-bounds and no backdrop → geometry visible + canvas clickable, no full-canvas takeover; (2) drag a file in and back out of the window without dropping → no residual highlight; (3) truly empty canvas → dropping a site plan still places the backdrop; (4) drag a file over a canvas that has geometry → the site stays visible under the translucent hint (light theme).
### B742 — Delete on a road silently no-ops for many clicks, then suddenly works `[Site Planner]` (bug) #site-planner #road #selection #persistence #ui  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-09 as "NEW-1"; provisional **B736**, renumbered **B742** — fast-moving concurrent `main` took B734–B741 + V250–V254 across several merges. Per repo precedent the code/tests/commit keep the provisional **B736** label; only the backlog + verification IDs bumped (→ B742 / V255). Branch `claude/road-delete-intermittent-tjrn4s`.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED + headless-verified this session; parks in ⏳ Verify (Verify: live — the cloud-sync half is signed-in only + a timing/persistence class) → V255.** Selecting a road and pressing/clicking Delete did nothing for ~20 tries, then one finally deleted it. Now a single Delete removes the selected road immediately (button OR keyboard) and never silently no-ops — if a delete can't proceed it visibly falls through to a whole-element delete, and a failed cloud save surfaces loudly.
- Verify: live
- Origin: filed 2026-07-09 from chat
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** searched Open / ⏳ Verify / Done (BACKLOG*.md + BACKLOG_OPEN.md) — **net-new**, no item covers this. Nearest prior art (NOT dupes): **B673** (element-sync loud-conflict + delete/edit matrix — the conflict *policy*, not this local-no-op/wedge); **B230/B718** (the control-point add/delete feature this bug was mis-firing through); **B372** (a deleted *site* resurrecting — different object, the localStorage unmount-flush).
- **AUDIT-FIRST — three real defects, code-confirmed (not the report's single guess):**
  1. **Road keyboard-Delete trap (primary).** With a road selected and an interior control point *armed* (`selVtx`), `SitePlanner.jsx:2697` routed Delete to `deleteVtx` and `return`ed unconditionally. `deleteVtx`'s road branch (`:3638-3660`) early-returned on a non-removable/**stale** index (endpoint, 2-pt min, or an index gone out-of-range after the road's geometry changed under the armed selection — e.g. a realtime refetch replaced `els`) **without clearing `selVtx`**. So every later Delete re-hit that branch and no-op'd until Escape / a background click reset `selVtx` — "then it finally worked."
  2. **Right-click menu deletes stale selection** (`:12494`): `setSel({kind:"el",id}); deleteSel()` — `deleteSel` reads a ref `setSel` hasn't synchronously updated, so it acted on the previous selection (wrong element, or a no-op).
  3. **Silent cloud-sync wedge** (`elementSync.js:205-230` + `elementApi.js`): the per-element commit had **no timeout**, so a hung `commit_elements` left the single `inflight` slot stuck TRUE forever — all element writes (incl. deletes) piled up unsent, badge stuck "saving", flooding out only when the stall cleared (the persistence-side "then it worked").
- **Fix:**
  - `deleteVtx` now returns a **boolean** (true only when it actually removed a point) and clears `selVtx`+`roadVtxSel` on every no-op/guard path; the keyboard branch (`:2697`) gained `&& deleteVtx(...)` so a no-op **falls through** to the whole-element `deleteSel()` — Delete is never a dead key.
  - `deleteSel(target)` accepts an optional explicit `{kind,id}` (guarded on `.kind` so the five bare `onClick={deleteSel}` buttons that pass an event still fall back to the live ref); the context menu passes the clicked id directly.
  - RoadVtx **drag-end** clears `selVtx`, so reshaping a control point and then pressing Delete deletes the whole road (a deliberate plain click on a dot still arms it for a targeted vertex-delete).
  - `commitElements`/`fetchElements` (`elementApi.js`) bounded by **`COMMIT_TIMEOUT_MS = 8000`** (AbortController + `Promise.race`, mirrors `PARCEL_FETCH_TIMEOUT_MS`) → a hung request resolves `{ok:false}` → `onTransportFailure` retries/backs off → after `maxAttempts` the state goes `failed` → the existing red "error"/Retry badge (LOUD-FAILURE). This also closes the resurrection window (a delete that never lands can no longer be silently rebuilt by a refetch).
- **Verified (sandbox/headless):** new `test/elementApi.test.js` cases (hung commit → `{ok:false, /timeout/}`; abort-signal wired through; hung fetch → ok:false) · full unit suite green (3164) · build green · MAP.md regenerated · **`e2e/element-delete.spec.js` (3 tests, LOGGED-OUT via "Start blank" + a real drawn centerline road, green in headless Chromium): panel "Delete element" removes the road and it stays gone after reload; keyboard Delete after arming an interior control point removes just that vertex (road survives, pts 4→3) then a second Delete removes the whole road — NO WEDGE; and reshape-drag a control point then Delete removes the whole road. 0 page errors.**
- **⏳ V255 (live, on planyr.io, SIGNED IN — the sandbox can't sign in):** the cloud-sync half only. Delete a road with cloud on → it persists and stays deleted across a tab-switch + reload (no resurrection); and on a genuinely slow/failed commit the sync badge flips to "error/Retry" (not stuck on "saving").

- **Verified (sandbox/headless):** `test/multiStyle.test.js` (20 cases) + `test/bugHuntGuards.test.js` B740 guard green; full suite green · lint 0 errors · build green · MAP regenerated · `ui-audit/verify-b740.mjs` drives the logged-out app 12/12 (3-element Shift toggle add/remove, "N selected" panel, opacity-restore-to-100% on all, per-member outlines, replace/clear, 0 page errors).
- **⏳ V253 (live, signed-in on planyr.io):** confirm a multi opacity/style edit PERSISTS across reload for a signed-in user (the auth-only cloud path can't be exercised logged-out; same write path single-element edits already use, so low-risk).

### B738 — Satellite/aerial basemap missing from PDF/PNG export (plan prints on a blank white background) `[Site Planner]` (bug) #site-planner #export #gis  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-09 as "NEW-1"; provisional **B735**, renumbered **B738** — concurrent `main` (PRs #557/#559/#560) took B734/B735/B736/B737 + V250/V251. Per repo precedent the code/tests/commit keep the provisional **B735** label; only the backlog + verification IDs bumped (→ B738 / V252). Branch `claude/pdf-export-cors-imagery-4l1f8d`.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED + headless-verified this session; parks in ⏳ Verify (Verify: live — PDF/export parity + GIS endpoint behavior, both mandatory-live classes) → V252.** With the satellite/aerial basemap on, Print/Download PDF (and Download PNG) produced the vectors on a blank white background — the imagery was dropped. The export now composites the on-screen aerial into the sheet, and a fetch that can't be inlined warns loudly instead of silently emitting a background-less file.
- Verify: live
- Origin: filed 2026-07-09 from chat
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** searched Open / ⏳ Verify / Done (BACKLOG*.md + BACKLOG_OPEN.md) — **net-new**, no existing item covers the aerial missing from the export. Nearest prior art to BUILD ON, NOT dupes: **B50** (Done — made a *tainted-canvas* export failure surface an alert instead of a silent no-op; this is a different, more common failure — a **dropped** image, not a thrown taint); **B202** (Done — time-boxed + parallelized `inlineImages` so a hung tile can't stall print prep; introduced the very `dropOnFail` that this bug turns silent); **B693** (the Off/Aerial/USGS basemap control). The chat's own "NEW-2/NEW-3" bullets were gotchas on this one item, not separate numbers.
- **AUDIT-FIRST — the chat's leading hypothesis (a CORS-tainted canvas swallowing a SecurityError) did NOT match the code.** The export does not rasterize the live Leaflet DOM; `buildExportSvg` clones ONLY `svgRef.current`. The live basemap is a **sibling `<div ref={geoWrapRef}>`** (Leaflet tiles, `data-export="skip"`, zIndex 0) that the SVG clone never captures. So the export's only aerial source was the persisted `underlay` `<image>`. Two ways that goes blank: (1) **basemap on with no `underlay`** (a located site whose from-map capture is absent, or the underlay removed) → the SVG had no aerial at all; (2) `underlay.src` is a remote ArcGIS `export` URL and `inlineImages(dropOnFail=true)` **silently dropped** it on any fetch hiccup → white background, no error (a LOUD-FAILURE violation). CORS itself is fine: `server.arcgisonline.com` `export` **and** `tile` endpoints return `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *` (curl-verified), so a plain `fetch` inlines cleanly to a data URL (no taint).
- **Fix (three parts):**
  1. **Capture the live basemap for the export.** New `SitePlanner.exportAerialForFrame(frame)`: when `origin && basemapOn`, synthesize a **frame-exact** aerial by requesting the ACTIVE source's `export` endpoint (`BASEMAPS[basemapSrc].export` — Esri or USGS) sized to the printed area, placed in the SAME feet frame as the parcels so it aligns pixel-for-pixel. This is the same technique the from-map underlay already uses — reused, not reinvented.
  2. **Geometry:** new pure `feetExtentToBbox(ext, lat0, lon0)` in `lib/arcgis.js` (planner feet → lon/lat bbox; +x EAST, +y SOUTH), which `aerialPlacement` reverses exactly (proven by a round-trip unit test). `buildExportSvg` now takes an `exportAerial` and draws `aerial = exportAerial || underlay` (so the dropped-screenshot / basemap-off paths are unchanged), tagging the `<image>` `data-export-aerial`.
  3. **LOUD-FAILURE:** `inlineImages` now returns `{ aerialDropped }`; `exportPDF`/`exportPNG` `flashWarn` the user ("⚠ Couldn't load the satellite imagery, so the PDF was exported without it…") on the **success path** (after the file downloads, so a later encode failure can't leave a contradictory toast), with the **`⚠` prefix that flips the banner to the red warning colour** (without it the notice rendered on the success-green — B341-class).
  4. **Extent unification (review-driven).** Both `buildExportSvg` and `exportAerialForFrame` now crop to ONE shared `exportFeetExtent(frame)` (frame → dev → parcels → underlay bounds), and a reliable data-URL underlay is drawn BENEATH the live synth as a fallback — so a dropped fetch can't regress a previously-good export to white.
- **Adversarial review (4-lens Workflow + per-finding verify) caught a real gap before merge:** the first cut returned `null` from `exportAerialForFrame` for a **parcels-only site** (deed imported, no massing yet) with no print frame, because it keyed on `devExtent()` alone (which ignores `parcels`) while `buildExportSvg` still framed the parcels — so that (very common) state *still* silently exported white. Part 4 above fixes it; a `test/bugHuntGuards.test.js` guard locks the shared-extent wiring so it can't regress.
- **Verified (sandbox/headless):** `test/aerialExport.test.js` (3 tests — `feetExtentToBbox` north/south orientation, exact round-trip through `aerialPlacement` reconstructing the feet extent, and the `maxPx` export-ceiling clamp) · new **B735 guard** in `test/bugHuntGuards.test.js` (shared `exportFeetExtent` + `data-export-aerial` marker + `aerialDropped` signal all present) · **`ui-audit/verify-aerial-export-cors.mjs` (real headless Chromium, runs the ACTUAL `inlineImages` loop): a cross-origin image served with `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *` (identical CORS to Esri — asserted live by curl in the same script) inlines to a data URL, does NOT taint the canvas, and rasterizes into the backdrop (100% non-white, high colour variety); an unreachable aerial URL sets `aerialDropped=true` and drops the `<image>` (the LOUD-FAILURE contract)** · existing `ui-audit/verify-pdf-export.mjs` still green (no regression) · full unit suite **3,151 green** · lint 0 errors · build green · MAP.md regenerated (new `arcgis.js` export). NOTE: the live Esri `export` fetch could not be exercised from the *sandbox* browser (the egress proxy resets headless Chromium's TLS tunnel to arcgisonline, and blocks `basemap.nationalmap.gov` outright — 403 CONNECT; curl over HTTP/1.1 reaches Esri). So **Esri CORS `*` is curl-verified; USGS is expected (stock ArcGIS Server defaults AllowedOrigins=*) but pending the live check** — and if USGS turns out non-CORS, the LOUD warning fires (no silent white). A real browser at planyr.io has no proxy.
- **⏳ V252 (live, on planyr.io):** locate a real site → confirm the satellite backdrop is ON → **Download PDF**: the imagery must be the background with parcels/setbacks/markups/massing on top (repeat with the print frame set, and once with the **USGS** source). Then **Download PNG** → same. Toggle the basemap OFF (or a dropped-screenshot underlay) → export still behaves as before. Optional: throttle/kill the network mid-export → the "couldn't load the satellite imagery" warning shows and the file still downloads (no silent white). Also spot-check that a placed site-plan overlay + the "Print overlay" toggle still composite correctly above the aerial.
