### B673 — Element-level sync, phase 4/5: loud-conflict surface + delete/edit matrix `[Site Planner]` (feature) #site-planner #ui #persistence  *(owner brief 2026-07-06, arrived as "NEW-4"; minted **B673** — see B671's renumber note. Branch `claude/site-elements-schema-sync-4p2x5b`.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED this session; parks in ⏳ Verify (Verify: live — conflict paths are two-session timing) → V230.** No overwrite is ever silent: both sides of a per-element collision get a toast naming who changed what, with **Show** (zoom-to-element + select) or **Restore** riding along. Whole-element granularity, last-write-wins, no field merging — non-blocking BY DESIGN because nothing is lost.
- Verify: live
- Origin: filed 2026-07-06 from chat
- **The matrix (pure, unit-tested — `lib/conflictToasts.js`):** edit-vs-edit → the losing tab re-commits (LWW) and reads "⟨element⟩ was also just edited by ⟨name⟩ — your version was kept"; the overwritten tab (a foreign rev inside the ~15s authored window) reads "⟨name⟩ changed ⟨element⟩ you just edited — their version is showing" (over-trigger inside the window is by design). Editing a deleted element → tombstone hit → the deletion shows on canvas + "⟨element⟩ was deleted by ⟨name⟩" with **Restore** (a new `restore` op: clears the tombstone, writes your data, new rev; racing a live row adopts THEIRS + a follow-up notice). Deleting a just-edited element → the delete re-applies at the fresh rev (delete wins, silent for the deleter); the editor's side gets the removal + supersede notice. Create-vs-create → impossible by construction (per-tab salted ids, B591) — telemetry assert only. Remote changes OUTSIDE the window stay quiet (that's just live sync).
- **Attribution (`lib/editorNames.js`):** self-uid → "you (another window)"; teammates via the SECURITY DEFINER `list_team_members` roster RPC (profiles RLS is own-row-only), cached per site session; roster miss → "a teammate", never blank. Element labels via `describeElement` — buildings by their on-canvas display number ("Building 3"), others by type/kind.
- **Toast component (`src/shared/ui/Toast.jsx`, reusable):** non-blocking stack, auto-dismiss 8s with HOVER-HOLD (mouse over pauses the timer), optional action button, cap 4 + "+n more", `role="status"`, theme tokens only, solid fill + weight (never faded text; amber accent bar — red stays reserved for genuine alert). MODULE-SCOPE components.
- **zoom-to-element:** new `zoomToElement(kind, id)` frames the element's bbox (the frameToActiveParcels math over `featBBox`) + selects it — no per-element zoom existed before.
- **Verified here (sandbox):** lint 0 · 2,852 tests (+17: the full matrix mapping both sides + quiet passes, restore op ok/conflict flows, name resolver cache/self/fallback, describeElement, toast pure helpers) · build green · headless smoke 3/3 (signed-out untouched).
- **⏳ V230 (live, two signed-in sessions):** same-element race both-sides toasts with correct names, restore end-to-end, delete-vs-edit supersede notice. Until B674 removes the lock, same-browser tabs can't race (read-only gate) — the matrix is reachable cross-DEVICE now and fully same-browser after B674; folded into the consolidated Cowork runbook (docs/COWORK-ELEMENT-SYNC-LIVE.md, lands with B674).
- **2026-07-07 Cowork run: NOT faithfully exercised** — both sessions were the same account, so the named-toast halves ("⟨name⟩ changed…") and the team-roster attribution never fired ("you (another window)" is the only reachable label same-account). Still ⏳ pending a run with a SECOND account on a team-shared site (the one owner-side input — see OWNER-TODO).
- DEDUPE-FIRST: net-new (see B670); B455 (Done) demanded loud+BLOCKING conflict handling under the old whole-doc model — this is its per-element successor, non-blocking because LWW + both sides told + Restore means nothing is lost.

### B674 — Element-level sync, phase 5/5: remove the edit lock — multi-writer cutover + presence pill `[Site Planner / Shell]` (feature) #site-planner #ui #persistence  *(owner brief 2026-07-06, arrived as "NEW-5"; minted **B674** — see B671's renumber note. Branch `claude/site-elements-schema-sync-4p2x5b`.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED this session; parks in ⏳ Verify (Verify: live — the full multi-writer matrix is inherently multi-session) → V231 + the consolidated Cowork runbook `docs/COWORK-ELEMENT-SYNC-LIVE.md` (V229–V231 in one sitting).** Cutover complete: with multi-writer ON (default) the planner never takes the per-plan editor lock — every tab and user edits concurrently through the rev-checked element path, and a header pill shows who's here.
- Verify: live
- Origin: filed 2026-07-06 from chat
- **Escape hatch (`lib/multiwriter.js`):** `MULTIWRITER_DEFAULT = true` + the localStorage override `planyr.multiwriter` = "off" restores the old single-active-editor behavior client-side — deliberately NO new build-time env var (the Cloudflare env-at-build failure pattern). Throwing/blocked storage falls back to the default.
- **Lock removal (minimal-diff by design):** under multi-writer the lock is simply NEVER ACQUIRED (`editorLock.setProject(null)`), so `readOnly` stays false and the read-only banner + takeOverEditing become unreachable dead paths — kept compiled-in to serve the `off` hatch through the ~30-day blob-backup soak, then deleted with the backup drop (OWNER-TODO carries the date). The `editorLock.js` MODULE stays regardless (doc-review consumes it).
- **B313 notice suppressed for the planner:** AppHeader gains a `multiEditOk` prop (default false — doc-review keeps its warning); the planner passes `multiwriterEnabled()`, which idles the `useMultiTab` hook entirely.
- **Presence (`lib/presencePill.js` + wiring):** Supabase Realtime Presence rides the SAME per-site element channel, keyed by uid (two windows of one account = one person) and tracking `{uid, name}` — display name from the profile, NEVER the email. The pure `presenceSummary` renders the pill only when someone else is here: "N here", names on hover ("You" first, "You (2 windows)" nuance), through AppHeader's existing `saveSlot` (zero header API change).
- **The brief's amendment flag, resolved:** the "banner-collapse/presence-pill item from the edit-lock-banner session" it says to amend **does not exist anywhere** (swept headings + full text + git log before phase 1). Nothing to amend — its presence-pill half IS this item; its read-only-banner half is dead under multi-writer. Closest relatives all Done: B313 (suppressed here for the planner), the B464–B468/B480 read-only-lockout cluster (unreachable with the lock never taken).
- **Verified here (sandbox):** lint 0 · 2,860 tests (+8: multiwriter flag precedence/hatch/blocked-storage; presenceSummary alone/two-people/window-collapse/sort+fallback) · build green · headless smoke 3/3 (signed-out untouched — presence and multi-writer are cloud-active concerns).
- **⏳ V231 (live, the FULL owner matrix):** two→three authenticated sessions on planyr.io — concurrent edits both persist; same-element race = both toasts, correct names; restore end-to-end; offline dirty-queue flush + rejoin consistency; refresh-mid-edit loses nothing; 30-element paste = one batch; the old conflict banner NEVER appears; no resurrection on a site with pre-migration deletedIds; the `multiwriter=off` hatch restores lock behavior; presence pill counts/names. Step-by-step in `docs/COWORK-ELEMENT-SYNC-LIVE.md` (also delivered to the owner for handoff to a Cowork session).
- **2026-07-07 Cowork run, partial:** **#12 (no lock / no read-only banner / no old conflict banner anywhere) ✅ observed working** across the whole sitting; both-halves-persist not exercised. **#13 pill FAILED for two same-account windows** — `presenceSummary` counted PEOPLE (presence keys), and both windows share one uid → no pill (metas:2 under one key confirmed live). **Fixed this session: the pill counts SESSIONS** — two windows of one account now read "2 here" ("You (2 windows)" on hover), matching the runbook's "a second profile/incognito window counts as a second session"; +2 tests. **#18 (signed-out cold start) FAILED → its own item B690 (fixed + sandbox-verified same session, see BACKLOG-DONE).** #14–17 not run; the full matrix re-runs per the updated runbook (needs the second account for the named-toast halves — see OWNER-TODO).
- DEDUPE-FIRST: net-new (see B670).

### B714 — Sharing a project silently REVERTS: any ordinary save from the owner's open tab overwrote `sites.team_id` back to null, locking the collaborator out `[Site Planner / Review / teams · RLS]` (bug — data-integrity class) #site-planner #persistence #auth  *(owner live repro 2026-07-08 with the Cowork session: right-clicked Goose Creek → Share to michael.butler@hillwood.com → the site APPEARED on the test account, then broke — red cloud, elements gone after reload, no conflict toasts. Cowork's DB forensics found team "HIP Houston" + both members present but 0 sites linked, and filed it as "Share never sets team_id" (their NEW-1). First minted **B692**, then **B714** — BOTH taken by concurrent sessions on successive merge-ins of `origin/main` (B692 = the husk-parcel root-cause fix; B714 = dock-high truck-court pricing); settled as **B714** = highest B# across both files (B714) + 1.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED + unit-verified this session; parks in ⏳ Verify (Verify: live — the share round-trip is two-account/auth-only) → V244.** Sharing now survives every save: the sharing pointer can only be changed by the explicit Share/unshare action, never by a content autosave.
- Verify: live
- Origin: filed 2026-07-08 from the owner's live session (Cowork brief NEW-1 + NEW-2)
- **AUDIT-FIRST — the reported diagnosis was half right; the code reality is worse and explains everything.** `lib/sharing.js` DOES set `sites.team_id` correctly (UPDATE by `group_id`; the row's `group_id` is populated; the owner passes the rehome-guard trigger) — that's why the site initially appeared on the test account. The real bug: **every ordinary content push re-stamped `team_id` from the client's IN-MEMORY model** (`cloudUpsertCore` + `keepaliveCloudPush` for `sites`; `upsertReviewCore` + `keepaliveFlushReview` for `doc_reviews`; `upsertFileFacts` for `file_facts`, whose filing callers never even carry a teamId → hard `null`). The owner's open Goose Creek tab predated the share, so its next autosave wrote `team_id: null` — silently unsharing (the B486 rehome guard deliberately exempts the OWNER, so it never fired; a signed-in tab never re-reads the store, so it never learned the share happened). Timeline confirmed live: team created 2026-06-24, both members admins; the site row rewritten to v61 the same night with `team_id` back at null.
- **Fix — team_id is write-isolated to the sharing flow, everywhere:** `siteRowFor` / `reviewRowFor` (new pure row builders) OMIT `team_id` on every update — CAS autosaves and unload keepalives physically cannot carry the sharing pointer anymore; a brand-NEW row (first insert) still stamps the model's teamId so a plan/review created inside a shared project is born shared. `upsertFileFacts` sends `team_id` only when a caller explicitly provides one (the plain-upsert update leg then leaves the column untouched). `slimForCloud` additionally strips `teamId`/`ownerId` from the stored jsonb — the columns are the single source of truth, overlaid onto models at read time (`cloudList`/`loadReview`), and this keeps `headerSig` share-neutral so the B672 unchanged-header skip still works on shared sites.
- **Cowork's NEW-2 (realtime RLS "leak") — resolved by the same root cause, no leak.** The test account saw the owner's building move BEFORE its lockout because at that moment the site WAS legitimately shared (team_id set, RLS satisfied); the subsequent autosave-revert then produced the red cloud (writes rejected) and empty reload (reads rejected). Supabase `postgres_changes` enforces RLS per-subscriber, and the un-share also kills the subscription's row visibility. The V244 run includes a sanity check on a genuinely-unshared site.
- **Follow-on (small, filed not lost):** a file FILED into an already-shared project lands with `team_id null` (fact-row callers don't know the project's team) until the next re-share stamps it — pre-existing behavior, now explicit. Fix later by resolving the project's live team at filing time.
- **Verified here (sandbox):** 8-test `test/teamShareGuard.test.js` pins the rule for every writer (update rows carry NO team_id key; insert rows inherit; slim jsonb stripped; headerSig share-neutral) · full suite green · build green.
- **Data heal (prod):** the owner's intended share re-applied after deploy — `sites.team_id = 454aa114…(HIP Houston)` restored on group `smqfy48tlk9j` (Goose Creek) via MCP SQL (rehome-guard trigger safely bypassed for the one maintenance UPDATE; re-verified after).
- **⏳ V244 (live, two accounts — both already exist):** see VERIFICATION.md.
- DEDUPE-FIRST: net-new (no prior B# covers the share flow or team_id write-isolation); DISTINCT from the concurrent **B692** (husk-parcel model sanitize — the other half of the same live run's findings); B486 (Done) is the non-owner rehome guard this bug walked around by BEING the owner. The same owner brief's NEW-3 = **B690**/**B692** (render guard + root cause, both shipped) and NEW-4 = **B672 (×2)** (fixed + merged 2026-07-08) — the live session ran on build 40884e6, which predates those fixes; no new numbers minted for them.

_(new `Verify: live` items land here after implementation.)_

## 🕓 Later / Roadmap

### B641 — Outfall intelligence: flowline + design-tailwater sourcing `[Site Planner / Stormwater]` (feature — umbrella; tier-2/3 screening slice SHIPPED with B636–B640)  *(owner brief 2026-07-03, arrived as "NEW-6" roadmap; owner then asked for the tractable slice in-session; first filed **B634**, RENUMBERED to **B641** on merge-in of `origin/main` — concurrent sessions took B629–B635; B641 = highest real B# across both files (B640) + 1. Code/harness keep the provisional B629-batch labels — see the B636 note in BACKLOG-DONE.md.)*
`[ ]` Source the receiving system's flowline + design-storm tailwater to move Regime-A coverage (B632) from assumption to sourced band. Confidence tiers: **(1) HCFCD effective HEC-RAS model extraction** (channel-bottom + WSEL by storm at the nearest cross-section — highest confidence; BLOCKER: external model acquisition + a HEC-RAS parser, own workstream), **(2) LiDAR ditch-bottom for open ditches** (3DEP) — ✅ **first slice shipped 2026-07-03**: `screenOutfall()` samples a 3DEP cross-profile through the nearest HCFCD channel unit (`ditchStats` invert/bank/depth) and renders the value-of-information line in the Regime-A banner ("assumed shallow outfall vs measured ditch depth — here's what to pull to confirm"); never auto-credited, **(3) storm-sewer GIS inverts** (COH `UN_Stormwater` already wired; HGL/surcharge caveat: a deep pipe invert with a high hydraulic grade line is Regime B, not A — needs invert-field probing on the geogimstest host), **(4) adjacent-plan OCR via Document Review** (BLOCKER: rides auto-filing). Output pattern stays value-of-information: "assumed shallow outfall = X% coverage; if the receiving channel is deep and unsubmerged, ~Y% — worth Z sf; here's what to pull to confirm." This is the substance of the `docs/ROADMAP.md` Tier-1 "storm outfall" item (annotated there; the rate-rules half = B636).

### B623 — User-editable schedule conventions (working week, holidays, month/year roll behavior) `[Scheduler]` (feature)  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-02 as "NEW-3", filed to Later/Roadmap by owner instruction — do NOT build until moved up; provisionally NEW-3/"B617", renumbered **B623** on the `origin/main` merge-in that took B615–B620; B623 = highest real B# across both files (B622) + 1)*
`[ ]` **Roadmap — sequence AFTER B621/B622 (the duration model + finish lock, in-code labels `B615`/`B616`) prove out.** A settings surface letting the user edit the schedule's own date conventions, extending the existing holiday-selection UI to also cover: (a) the **working week** — e.g. enable **6-day weeks** (B621 hard-codes the week to 5 working days; this makes it editable), and optionally (b) the **month/year roll behavior** (the plain-forward roll B621 fixed). Reasonable extension since holiday selection already exists (`ensureHolidays` / `HOLIDAY_SET` in `public/sequence/index.html`). **Same loud/visible discipline as the rest of the schedule:** the working week and roll direction silently change every derived date, so any change must **re-run cascade and SURFACE the shifted dates** (before/after diff, same discipline as B621's migration), never move them quietly. Depends on the B621 duration model (week-factor is currently the hard-coded `DUR_WD_FACTOR.w = 5` + the weekend test inside `addBD`/`workdaysBetween`/`rollForwardToWorkday` — those become the parameterized seam) and the B622 conflict-surfacing pattern (reuse the banner/row-flag). **Do NOT parameterize the week inside B621** — that was deliberately deferred here.

### B371 — GIS screening cache Phase 2: regional Houston-metro snapshot / offline pre-cache `[Site Planner / Analysis]` (feature) — Phase 2 of B367  *(filed 2026-06-22; minted **B371**)*
`[ ]` **Later (gated behind B367 Phase 1, which shipped).** Phase 1 (B367) keeps the last-good answer per parcel+layer and never blanks a layer on a transient outage. Phase 2 is the owner's "cache most of Houston" idea: a **regional pre-cache/snapshot** of the Houston-metro source layers (+ a coverage mask), refreshed on a schedule, so a **never-seen** parcel with no features resolves **offline** to "No <layer> mapped (source vintage <date>)" instead of waiting on (or failing) a live query. Heavier — needs storage (a Supabase table or a static snapshot) + a refresh job + a coverage mask so "no features in the snapshot" is trustworthy only inside the cached extent. Deferred deliberately behind Phase 1 per the brief; pick up once Phase 1 proves out in the field.

### B340 — Auto-assembly CV tails behind the B335–B339 seams `[Doc Review / Stitch]` (feature) — the hard minority  *(filed 2026-06-21 as the deferred remainder of the B335–B339 batch; minted **B340** — a hot `main` took B325–B334)*
`[ ]` The B335–B339 headline flow (drop a set → auto-group → auto-stitch → crop → auto-calibrate) is **shipped + verified** for the common case — CAD vector PDFs with a real text layer. (Scanned-sheet **OCR** was the 4th tail and is now **DONE → B352**, shipped + verified this session.) Three computer-vision tails remain, deferred behind clean injectable seams because each needs vector-graphics analysis we can't yet headless-verify — and the manual-Align safety net already covers them:
  1. **Graphic scale-bar reading (B339 tail)** — when there's no stated scale text, measure the drawn scale bar to set `ftPerUnit`. Needs vector-graphics/CV analysis, not text.
  2. **Geometric edge-line match (B337 middle fallback)** — when match-line *labels* are missing, match the cut geometry across two sheets' edges. Today, label-less sheets correctly drop to the 2-point manual Align **pre-seeded** with detected seam endpoints (the spec's final safety net, already wired) — this is the CV step between labels and manual.
  3. **Legend symbol-union (B338 tail)** — extract each sheet's graphical legend entries and union them into the pinned Composite key (today the key lists the grouped plan + auto-scale; the crop + pinned panel ship). Needs symbol/vector extraction.
> Each is gated behind a seam exactly like the app's other not-yet-provisioned heavy compute (the AI title-block reader, the APS converter). Pick up when there's a way to verify (a CV pass we can headless-check). Coupled to the ★ north-star "map → drawings → latest set."
>
> **AMENDMENT 2026-07-03 (owner pulled the CV tails into active scope, Cowork brief) — the PURE ENGINES for all three now ship + are unit-tested; the browser EXTRACTION + live verification remain.** These reduce manual-Align on *real* plan sets; they do **NOT** fix the JACINTOPORT schedule-set wall (that was B630–B633). What landed this session:
> 1. **Graphic scale-bar reading** — `src/shared/files/scaleBarRead.js` (`readScaleBar` + `clusterBars`/`ticksNearBar`/`tickLinearity`), wired fail-open via `sheetRead.scaleBarCalibration` as a fallback in `groupCalibration` (stated scale still wins). Reads a drawn bar's geometry + tick labels → `feetPerUnit`; only applies on a high-confidence, feet-unit read, never over a stated/manual cal.
> 2. **Geometric edge-line match** — `src/shared/files/edgeGeomMatch.js` (`fitEdgeLine` PCA/total-least-squares + `orderEndpoints` + `matchSeamEdges`), wired fail-open via `autoStitch.seamEndpointsFor` (prefers a drawn seam's geometry over the rectangle edge; improve-only, keeps the pre-seeded 2-point net). The vector path complementing the raster fitter (`matchLineFit.js`, B413).
> 3. **Legend symbol-union** — `src/shared/files/legendUnion.js` (`unionLegendEntries` + `legendFromPlaced`), wired into the Stitcher Composite key (rendered only when non-empty).
> **STILL OPEN (why this stays here):** each engine consumes geometry that a **browser vector/CV extractor must supply** — the `scaleBar` fact, per-sheet `seamGeom`, and per-sheet `legendEntries` — and **nothing populates those seams yet**, so all three are **dormant / zero behavior change today** (dormant exactly like the OCR/APS seams). None can be headless-verified → the extraction + real-browser proof on the owner's sets is **V201**. Fail open throughout; never present a topology-only placement as "aligned."

### B256 — Scheduler recompute is O(n²); will lag past ~500 tasks `[Scheduler / perf]` (task)  *(orig "P2"; minted **B256**)*
`[ ]` `cascadeDates`/`rollupParentDates` re-filter the task list repeatedly on each edit; `depLines` calls `tasks.indexOf` inside its loop; `rolledHealthMap`/`progressMap` recurse with `.filter`. Fine at the current ~180 tasks; will start to feel laggy past ~500. Fix: build an `id → index` map and a `parent → children[]` map once per recompute and reuse them — behaviour-preserving. **Verify** every task's start/end/duration is byte-identical before/after on the real production dataset. Gated by board size → Later until a board actually grows that large.

### B272 — Rule out a main-thread stall from non-Workerized heavy parsing `[Core / Site Planner]` (bug, low priority)  *(owner-dropped 2026-06-20 via chat; arrived as "NEW-2"; minted **B272** — secondary hypothesis to B271)*
`[ ]` Secondary hypothesis for the same "unclickable canvas" symptom: heavy CAD/PDF parse (or other compute) running on the **main thread** instead of a Web Worker, jamming the tab. **Investigated 2026-06-20 (B271 session):** PDF parsing already runs **off** the main thread — PDF.js uses its worker (a separate `pdf.worker` chunk in the build); DWG→DXF conversion is a **backend** (`/server`) concern, never in the browser. The reported incident's symptom (a frozen grab/hand cursor + clicks swallowed, with **no** Chrome "Page Unresponsive — Wait/Exit" prompt) is the signature of stuck pointer state, not a CPU stall, and is fully explained + fixed by **B271**. **No actionable main-thread-stall bug found.** Per the owner's note this drops to **low priority** now that B271 resolves the lockout — kept here (not closed) so it stays on the radar. **Escalate only** if an actual stall is ever observed: then instrument long-task timing, reproduce with a large drawing, and move any straggler heavy compute into a Worker per the standing architecture rule.

- **Enforced merge gate via GitHub branch protection** (the settings half of **B63**): require a PR + a passing build check + "branch up to date before merging" on `main`, plus repo auto-merge. On the **private** repo this only *enforces* on a paid plan (GitHub Pro+); on Free the rules save but don't block — so B63's branch → PR → green discipline is the backstop until then. Keep it a manual owner toggle rather than granting the Claude Code app admin rights on a credential-bound repo.

- **B150 — Wire dedicated county appraisal districts (CADs) for the Austin & DFW metros** `[Site Planner / map]` (feature) — *filed 2026-06-18 as a later-feature note (owner asked to park it).* Today only **Harris / Fort Bend / Chambers** have dedicated CADs in `lib/counties.js` (`COUNTIES` + `COUNTIES_MAP`). Austin (Travis/**TCAD**, Williamson, Hays) and DFW (Tarrant/**TAD**, Dallas/**DCAD**, Denton, Collin) parcels currently work **only via the statewide TxGIO fallback** (B137) — coverage is complete (verified: Travis 835K, Tarrant 757K, Dallas 694K, Williamson/Hays/Denton/Collin all present) and returns owner/situs/market-value/acreage, but the statewide copy can **lag** a county's live CAD and carries a **thinner field set** than the district's own service. Wire each county's dedicated CAD (verify it publishes a reachable, **CORS-clean** parcel service first — same vetting as the ETJ sources; some counties publish cleanly, some don't) so Austin/DFW get the same first-class, most-current parcel/appraisal data Houston has via HCAD/FBCAD; add per-county bbox routing to `candidateCountiesForPoint` as each lands.
  - **Bundle the county-mislabel fix:** a parcel in a non-configured county is presently tagged `chambers` (the statewide source's key) because the **B36(a)** `countyAtPoint` relabel only maps to the 3 wired CAD keys — so an Austin/DFW lot saves with the wrong `county`. Record the **true** county name even when no dedicated CAD is wired (cosmetic today; matters for the saved Site Model + which jurisdiction defaults show).
  - Coupled to **B11 / B13 / B36 / B137** (the county-resolution theme). **Not urgent** — the statewide fallback keeps Austin/DFW functional meanwhile; pick up when the owner is actively working those metros (start with Travis, Tarrant, Dallas).
